  • Agent (2024-06-05 22:06:37.499197): This is a powerful and inspiring quote from Nelson Mandela. Here are a few key points about it:

    - It acknowledges that failure and setbacks are an inevitable part of life. The phrase "never falling" suggests a perfection that is not realistic for anyone.

    - However, the quote emphasizes that the true test of character is not in avoiding failure, but in how we respond to it. "Rising every time we fall" speaks to resilience, perseverance, and an indomitable spirit.

    - "The greatest glory" frames this ability to overcome adversity as the highest achievement and most admirable quality one can demonstrate in life. It's not about a perfect record, but about the courage to always get back up.

    - Coming from Nelson Mandela, these words carry extra weight. He faced immense struggles and setbacks in his long fight against apartheid, including 27 years in prison, before becoming South Africa's first black head of state. His life exemplifies the message of the quote.

    In summary, this memorable statement is a reminder that our lowest moments do not define us - it's our determination to move past them that reveals our true strength and leads to our greatest triumphs. It's a call to be resilient in the face of life's inevitable challenges.

    1. Decide what kind of chicken you want - there are many breeds available for different purposes like egg laying, meat production, or as pets. Some common breeds include Rhode Island Reds, Orpingtons, and Silkies.

    2. Find a reputable breeder, hatchery or farm supply store in your area that sells chickens. You can search online or ask for recommendations from other chicken owners.

    3. Contact the seller to check availability of the breed you want and at what age/size they sell them (day-old chicks, started pullets, full grown, etc). Ask about the price per bird.

    4. Prepare a proper brooder setup for a young chick with a heat lamp, bedding, chick feed, and water before bringing your chicken home. For older birds, have a coop and run area ready.

    5. Pick up your chicken or have it shipped to you. Transport it home carefully in a ventilated box or carrier.

    6. Quarantine new birds from any existing flock for 30 days to prevent potential disease spread. Provide your chicken a healthy diet, clean living space, and veterinary care as needed.

    Let me know if you have any other questions! Raising backyard chickens can be a fun and rewarding experience.
